<hr>
<p>This package should work on both Julia 0.6 and 0.7, but it is dramatically (&gt;2x) faster on 0.7 on my test computer.
I need clean up the interface, and want to add a few basic LAPACK type functions.
I should also probably add more thorough tests; currently they just loop through a lot of matrix operations.
They take some time to run. Compile time subjectively doesn't seem too bad for multiplication, but I'm sure it could be improved.</p>
<p>The tests seem to randomly segfault after a while, and I am not sure why. Could I be filling up the methods table?
Either way, may be good to cull the amount of things that are parametrically typed.</p>
<p><code>getindex</code> and show methods, however, do not do well.</p>
<p>Regarding LAPACK functionality, I intend to add Cholesky decompositions, triangular matrix inversions, symm, and trmm functions.
That was the origin of the original name of this library (TriangularMatrices). That name will probably change.</p>
<p>For <code>gemm</code> type operations <code>D = A*X</code>, it is optimized fairly well for <code>A</code> having a multiple of 8 rows.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-julia"><pre><span class="pl-k">using</span> TriangularMatrices, BenchmarkTools
a8 <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">randmat</span>(<span class="pl-c1">8</span>);
x8_4 <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">randmat</span>(<span class="pl-c1">8</span>,<span class="pl-c1">4</span>);
d8_4 <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">randmat</span>(<span class="pl-c1">8</span>,<span class="pl-c1">4</span>);

TriangularMatrices<span class="pl-k">.</span><span class="pl-c1">mul!</span>(d8_4, a8, x8_4)

<span class="pl-k">using</span> BenchmarkTools
<span class="pl-c1">@benchmark</span> TriangularMatrices<span class="pl-k">.</span><span class="pl-c1">mul!</span>(<span class="pl-k">$</span>d8_4, <span class="pl-k">$</span>a8, <span class="pl-k">$</span>x8_4)

<span class="pl-c1">@code_llvm</span> TriangularMatrices<span class="pl-k">.</span><span class="pl-c1">mul!</span>(d8_4, a8, x8_4)
<span class="pl-c1">@code_native</span> TriangularMatrices<span class="pl-k">.</span><span class="pl-c1">mul!</span>(d8_4, a8, x8_4)</pre></div>
<p>The underlying data layout is recursive. You can visualize this via:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-julia"><pre>rm <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">RecursiveMatrix</span><span class="pl-c1">{Float64,50,50,50^2}</span>();
<span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">set_to_ind!</span>(A)
    <span class="pl-c1">@inbounds</span> <span class="pl-k">for</span> i <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-k">:</span><span class="pl-c1">length</span>(A)
        A[i] <span class="pl-k">=</span> i
    <span class="pl-k">end</span>
    A
<span class="pl-k">end</span>
<span class="pl-c1">set_to_ind!</span>(rm)</pre></div>
<p>One long term plan is to add plenty of smoke and mirror / convenience functions that abstract away the memory layout, and make iteration easy.
If one doesn't mix these with normal arrays, differences in underlying memory layout shouldn't be an issue.</p>
<p>Major problems right now are that printing and Cartesian getindex style functions do not seem to work for sizes &gt; 100; the computer just hangs.
I am not sure why. The sub2ind function seems to work fine, and switching from the generated function did not help.</p>
<p>At small sizes, we have the option of generating StaticArrays.
Note that the API is likely to change (improve) all around, and anything on that front is welcome. More <code>StaticArrays.jl</code> like.
For now, because they were easy to implement,</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-julia"><pre>julia<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-k">using</span> StaticArrays, TriangularMatrices, BenchmarkTools

<p>I wont promise better performance in general. Perhaps I should push some of these methods to <code>StaticArrays.jl</code> (but they may need testing beyond Ryzen), and I'd invite anyone from <code>StaticArrays.jl</code> to feel free to make use of the code included here.
The reason I haven't immediately pushed, however, is that my style of creating generated functions is very different (and much more verbose) than that from <code>StaticArrays</code>.
It performs best when there is a multiple of 8 rows for matrix <code>a</code>. Transposes are currently not supported.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-julia"><pre>julia<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span> a9_7_t <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">srandmat</span>(<span class="pl-c1">9</span>,<span class="pl-c1">7</span>);

<p>The particular case of 8 rows is used as a computational kernel for operations on larger matrices. These larger matrices have the recurse memory layout (the statically sized ones are column major). I use <code>unsafe_convert</code> on the pointer to the matrices, to convert the pointer to one of a StaticRecursiveMatrix, and then <code>unsafe_load</code> it, perform some matrix operations, and then <code>unsafe_store!</code>.</p>
<p>The recursive memory layout helps with memory locality. We take successively smaller blocks, until we are within 3x the cutoff (8), and then calculate the matrix product of these smaller blocks, that should fit reasonably well in cache. The submatrices we load, and apply the well optimized (at least for the one test CPU) kernel to, are all contiguous within the larger matrices -- and therefore easy to load.
Loading a block from a more typical column or row major matrix means loading data that is [matrix stride] apart.</p>
<p>Currently only "reasonably square" matrices are supported (those that wont become more square by dividing the larger dimension by 2); the next couple updates will probably add unsquare ones. I just didn't implement the recursion pattern yet for when we aren't subdividing both matrices into 4 pieces.</p>
<p>Work must still be done -- but it is pretty fast, and seems to hold on well!
Disclaimer is that (again), this has only been tested on one CPU</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-julia"><pre>julia<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">versioninfo</span>()

<p>In my opinion, this is holding on really well.
Too bad printing is much more complicated than matrix multiplication, but I'm sure I can figure that out someday.</p>
<p>Of course, with threading OpenBLAS would do increasingly well starting at these sizes.
Once Julia's threading is reworked, it would probably be worth handing here.</p>
